<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt358" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"see also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Dog behavior#Behavior compared with other canids"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAfo"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt358" id="mwAfs">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dog_behavior#Behavior_compared_with_other_canids" title="Dog behavior">Dog behavior §<span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span>Behavior compared with other canids</a></div>

codecs="vp8, vorbis"' data-width="1920" data-height="1080" data-title="Full HD WebM (1080P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 1080P" id="mwAgw"/></video></span><figcaption id="mwAg0">Dog swimming over to catch a ball, pay attention to the leg and tail movements</figcaption></figure>
<p id="mwAg4">Dog behavior is the internally coordinated responses (actions or inactions) of the domestic dog (individuals or groups) to internal and external stimuli.<sup about="#mwt364" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-levitis2009_58-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"levitis2009"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-levitis2009-58" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 58;" id="mwAg8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAhA">[58]</span></a></sup> As the oldest domesticated species, dogs' minds inevitably have been shaped by millennia of contact with humans. As a result of this physical and social evolution, dogs have acquired the ability to understand and communicate with humans more than any other species and they are uniquely attuned to human behaviors.<sup about="#mwt365" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-berns2012_13-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"berns2012"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-berns2012-13" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 13;" id="mwAhE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAhI">[13]</span></a></sup> Behavioral scientists have uncovered a surprising set of social-cognitive abilities in domestic dogs. These abilities are not possessed by the dog's closest canine relatives or other highly intelligent mammals, such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Great_ape" title="Great ape" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAhM">great apes</a>, but rather parallel to children's social-cognitive skills.<sup about="#mwt366" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-tomasello2009_59-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"tomasello2009"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-tomasello2009-59" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 59;" id="mwAhQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAhU">[59]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAhY">Unlike other domestic species selected for production-related traits, dogs were initially selected for their behaviors.<sup about="#mwt377" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-60" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-60"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-60" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 60;" id="mwAhc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAhg">[60]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt378" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-cagan2016_61-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"cagan2016"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-cagan2016-61" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 61;" id="mwAhk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAho">[61]</span></a></sup> In 2016, a study found that only 11 fixed genes showed variation between wolves and dogs.<sup about="#mwt382" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-62" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-62"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-62" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 62;" id="mwAhs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAhw">[62]</span></a></sup> These gene variations were unlikely to have been the result of natural evolution and indicate selection on both morphology and behavior during dog domestication. These genes have been shown to affect the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Catecholamine#Synthesis" title="Catecholamine" id="mwAh0">catecholamine synthesis</a> pathway, with the majority of the genes affecting the fight-or-flight response<sup about="#mwt383" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-cagan2016_61-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"cagan2016"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-cagan2016-61" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 61;" id="mwAh4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAh8">[61]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt384" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-63" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-63"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-63" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 63;" id="mwAiA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAiE">[63]</span></a></sup> (i.e., selection for tameness) and emotional processing.<sup about="#mwt385" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-cagan2016_61-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"cagan2016"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-cagan2016-61" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 61;" id="mwAiI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAiM">[61]</span></a></sup> Dogs generally show reduced fear and aggression compared with wolves.<sup about="#mwt386" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-cagan2016_61-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"cagan2016"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-cagan2016-61" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 61;" id="mwAiQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAiU">[61]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt387" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-64" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-64"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-64" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 64;" id="mwAiY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAic">[64]</span></a></sup> Some of these genes have been associated with aggression in some dog breeds, indicating their importance in both the initial domestication and later in breed formation.<sup about="#mwt391" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-cagan2016_61-4" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"cagan2016"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-cagan2016-61"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-cagan2016-61" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 61;" id="mwAig"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAik">[61]</span></a></sup> Traits of high sociability and lack of fear in dogs may include genetic modifications related to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Williams-Beuren_syndrome" title="Williams-Beuren syndrome" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAio">Williams-Beuren syndrome</a> in humans, which cause <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hypersociability" title="Hypersociability" id="mwAis">hypersociability</a> at the expense of problem-solving ability.<sup about="#mwt395" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-sciencemag_65-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"sciencemag"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-sciencemag-65"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-sciencemag-65" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 65;" id="mwAiw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAi0">[65]</span></a></sup></p>

<section data-mw-section-id="17" id="mwAi4"><h3 id="Intelligence">Intelligence</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt396" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Dog intelligence"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAi8"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt396" id="mwAjA">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dog_intelligence" title="Dog intelligence">Dog intelligence</a></div>

<p id="mwAjE">Dog intelligence is the dog's ability to perceive information and retain it as knowledge for applying to solve problems. Studies of two dogs suggest that dogs can learn by inference and have advanced memory skills.  A study with <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Rico_(Border_Collie)" title="Rico (Border Collie)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAjI">Rico</a>, a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Border_Collie" title="Border Collie" id="mwAjM">Border Collie</a>, showed that he knew the labels of over 200 different items. He inferred the names of novel things by exclusion learning and correctly retrieved those new items immediately and four weeks after the initial exposure. A study of another Border Collie, Chaser, documented his learning and memory capabilities. He had learned the names and could associate by verbal command over 1,000 words.<sup about="#mwt403" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-66" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-66"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-66" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 66;" id="mwAjQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAjU">[66]</span></a></sup> Dogs can read and react appropriately to human body language such as gesturing and pointing and human voice commands.</p>

<p id="mwAjY">One study of canine cognitive abilities found that dogs' capabilities are no more exceptional than those of other animals, such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Horse" title="Horse" id="mwAjc">horses</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Common_chimpanzee" title="Common chimpanzee" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAjg">chimpanzees</a>, or <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cat" title="Cat" id="mwAjk">cats</a>.<sup about="#mwt406" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Lea2018_67-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Lea2018"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Lea2018-67" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 67;" id="mwAjo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAjs">[67]</span></a></sup> One limited study of 18 household dogs found that they lacked spatial memory, and were more focussed on the "what" of a task rather than the "where".<sup about="#mwt407" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sluka2018_68-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sluka2018"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Sluka2018-68" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 68;" id="mwAjw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAj0">[68]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAj4">Dogs demonstrate a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Theory_of_mind" title="Theory of mind" id="mwAj8">theory of mind</a> by engaging in deception.<sup about="#mwt414" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-69" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-69"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-69" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 69;" id="mwAkA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAkE">[69]</span></a></sup> An experimental study showed compelling evidence that Australian <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dingo" title="Dingo" id="mwAkI">dingos</a> can outperform domestic dogs in non-social problem-solving, indicating that domestic dogs may have lost much of their original problem-solving abilities once they joined humans.<sup about="#mwt418" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-70" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-70"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-70" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 70;" id="mwAkM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAkQ">[70]</span></a></sup> Another study revealed that after undergoing training to solve a simple manipulation task, dogs faced with an unsolvable version of the same problem look at the human, while socialized wolves do not.<sup about="#mwt422" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-71" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-71"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-71" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 71;" id="mwAkU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAkY">[71]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="18" id="mwAkc"><h3 id="Communication">Communication</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt423" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Dog communication"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAkg"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt423" id="mwAkk">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dog_communication" title="Dog communication">Dog communication</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1134653256" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" about="#mwt426" </div><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Articles_with_hAudio_microformats" about="#mwt426" id="mwAks"/>

<p id="mwAkw">Dog communication is how dogs convey information to other dogs, understand messages from humans and translate the information that dogs are transmitting.<sup about="#mwt435" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-72" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-72"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-72" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 72;" id="mwAk0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAk4">[72]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap" about="#mwt434" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"rp","href":"./Template:Rp"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"xii"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAk8"><span title="Page / location: xii"><span typeof="mw:Entity">:</span><span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span>xii<span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span></span></sup> Communication behaviors of dogs include eye gaze, facial expression, vocalization, body posture (including movements of bodies and limbs), and gustatory communication (scents, pheromones, and taste). Humans communicate to dogs by using vocalization, hand signals, and body posture.</p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="19" id="mwAlA"><h2 id="Ecology">Ecology</h2>
<section data-mw-section-id="20" id="mwAlE"><h3 id="Population">Population</h3>
<p id="mwAlI">The dog is probably the most widely abundant large <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Carnivora" title="Carnivora" id="mwAlM">carnivoran</a> living in the human environment.<sup about="#mwt441" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-:0_73-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":":0"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-:0-73"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-:0-73" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 73;" id="mwAlQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAlU">[73]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt445" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-74" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-74"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-74" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 74;" id="mwAlY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAlc">[74]</span></a></sup>
In 2013, the estimated global dog population was between 700 million<sup about="#mwt454" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-75" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-75"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-75" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 75;" id="mwAlg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAlk">[75]</span></a></sup> and 987 million.<sup about="#mwt458" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-76" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-76"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-76" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 76;" id="mwAlo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAls">[76]</span></a></sup> About 20% of dogs live as pets in developed countries.<sup about="#mwt459" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Lord2013_77-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Lord2013"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Lord2013-77" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 77;" id="mwAlw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAl0">[77]</span></a></sup> In the developing world, dogs are typically feral or communally owned, with pet dogs uncommon. Most of these dogs live their lives as scavengers and have never been owned by humans, with one study showing their most common response when approached by strangers is to run away (52%) or respond aggressively (11%).<sup about="#mwt463" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-78" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-78"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-78" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 78;" id="mwAl4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAl8">[78]</span></a></sup> Little is known about these dogs, or the dogs in developed countries that are feral, strays, or are in shelters because the great majority of modern research on dog cognition has focused on pet dogs living in human homes.<sup about="#mwt467" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-79" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-79"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-79" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 79;" id="mwAmA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAmE">[79]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="21" id="mwAmI"><h3 id="Competitors_and_predators">Competitors and predators</h3>
<p id="mwAmM">Although dogs are the most abundant and widely distributed terrestrial carnivores, feral and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Free-ranging_dogs" title="Free-ranging dogs" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAmQ">free-ranging dogs' potential</a> to compete with other large carnivores is limited by their strong association with humans.<sup about="#mwt475" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-:0_73-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":":0"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-:0-73" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 73;" id="mwAmU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAmY">[73]</span></a></sup> For example, a review of the studies in dogs' competitive effects on <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sympatry" title="Sympatry" id="mwAmc">sympatric</a> carnivores did not mention any research on competition between dogs and wolves.<sup about="#mwt476" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-lescureaux2014_80-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"lescureaux2014"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-lescureaux2014-80" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 80;" id="mwAmg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAmk">[80]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt477" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-vanak2014_81-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"vanak2014"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-vanak2014-81" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 81;" id="mwAmo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAms">[81]</span></a></sup> Although wolves are known to kill dogs, they tend to live in pairs or in small packs in areas where they are highly persecuted, giving them a disadvantage facing large dog groups.<sup about="#mwt478" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-lescureaux2014_80-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"lescureaux2014"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-lescureaux2014-80" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 80;" id="mwAmw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAm0">[80]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt472" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoitaniMech2003259–264_82-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Boitani"},"2":{"wt":"Mech"},"3":{"wt":"2003"},"pp":{"wt":"259–264"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoitaniMech2003259–264-82" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 82;" id="mwAm4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAm8">[82]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAnA">Wolves kill dogs wherever they are found together.<sup about="#mwt481" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoitaniMech2003305–306_83-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Boitani"},"2":{"wt":"Mech"},"3":{"wt":"2003"},"pp":{"wt":"305–306"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoitaniMech2003305–306-83" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 83;" id="mwAnE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAnI">[83]</span></a></sup> In some instances, wolves have displayed an uncharacteristic fearlessness of humans and buildings when attacking dogs to the extent that they have to be beaten off or killed.<sup about="#mwt487" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-84" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-84"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-84" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 84;" id="mwAnM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAnQ">[84]</span></a></sup> Although the numbers of dogs killed each year are relatively low, it induces a fear of wolves entering villages and farmyards to take dogs and losses of dogs to wolves have led to demands for more liberal wolf hunting regulations.<sup about="#mwt488" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-lescureaux2014_80-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"lescureaux2014"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-lescureaux2014-80" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 80;" id="mwAnU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAnY">[80]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAnc"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Coyote" title="Coyote" id="mwAng">Coyotes</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Big_cat" title="Big cat" id="mwAnk">big cats</a> have also been known to attack dogs. In particular, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Leopard" title="Leopard" id="mwAno">leopards</a> are known to have a preference for dogs and have been recorded to kill and consume them, no matter what their size.<sup about="#mwt495" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Leopard_85-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Leopard"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Leopard-85"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Leopard-85" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 85;" id="mwAns"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAnw">[85]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Siberian_tiger" title="Siberian tiger" id="mwAn0">Siberian tigers</a> in the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amur_river" title="Amur river" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAn4">Amur River</a> region have killed dogs in the middle of villages. This indicates that the dogs were targeted. Amur tigers will not tolerate wolves as competitors within their territories, and the tigers could be considering dogs in the same way.<sup about="#mwt496" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Gompper2013_86-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Gompper2013"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Gompper2013-86" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 86;" id="mwAn8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAoA">[86]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Striped_hyena" title="Striped hyena" id="mwAoE">Striped hyenas</a> are known to kill dogs in their range.<sup about="#mwt500" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Striped_87-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Striped"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Striped-87"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Striped-87" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 87;" id="mwAoI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAoM">[87]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="22" id="mwAoQ"><h3 id="Diet">Diet</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt501" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"See also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Dog food"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAoU"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt501" id="mwAoY">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dog_food" title="Dog food">Dog food</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwAoc"><a href="./File:Golden_retriever_eating_pigs_foot.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwAog"><img resource="./File:Golden_retriever_eating_pigs_foot.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Golden_retriever_eating_pigs_foot.jpg/170px-Golden_retriever_eating_pigs_foot.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="659" data-file-type="bitmap" height="224" width="170" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Golden_retriever_eating_pigs_foot.jpg/255px-Golden_retriever_eating_pigs_foot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Golden_retriever_eating_pigs_foot.jpg/340px-Golden_retriever_eating_pigs_foot.jpg 2x" id="mwAok"/></a><figcaption id="mwAoo">A <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Golden_Retriever" title="Golden Retriever" id="mwAos">Golden Retriever</a> gnawing on a pig's foot</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwAow">Dogs have been described as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Omnivore" title="Omnivore" id="mwAo0">omnivores</a>.<sup about="#mwt510" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-ADW_12-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"ADW"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-ADW-12" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 12;" id="mwAo4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAo8">[12]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt514" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-88" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-88"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-88" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 88;" id="mwApA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwApE">[88]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt518" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-89" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-89"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-89" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 89;" id="mwApI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwApM">[89]</span></a></sup> Compared to wolves, dogs from agricultural societies have <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amylase#Evolution" title="Amylase" id="mwApQ">extra copies of amylase</a> and other genes involved in starch digestion that contribute to an increased ability to thrive on a starch-rich diet.<sup about="#mwt519" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-axelssonetal2013_11-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"axelssonetal2013"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-axelssonetal2013-11" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 11;" id="mwApU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwApY">[11]</span></a></sup> Similar to humans, some dog breeds produce amylase in their <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Saliva" title="Saliva" id="mwApc">saliva</a> and are classified as having a high starch diet.<sup about="#mwt526" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Pajic2019_90-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Pajic2019"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Pajic2019-90"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Pajic2019-90" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 90;" id="mwApg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwApk">[90]</span></a></sup> However, more like cats and less like other omnivores, dogs can only produce <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bile_acid" title="Bile acid" id="mwApo">bile acid</a> with <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Taurine" title="Taurine" id="mwAps">taurine</a> and they cannot produce <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vitamin_D" title="Vitamin D" id="mwApw">vitamin D</a>, which they obtain from animal flesh. Also more like cats, dogs require <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Arginine" title="Arginine" id="mwAp0">arginine</a> to maintain its nitrogen balance. These nutritional requirements place dogs halfway between carnivores and omnivores.<sup about="#mwt530" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-91" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-91"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-91" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 91;" id="mwAp4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAp8">[91]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="23" id="mwAqA"><h3 id="Range">Range</h3>
<p id="mwAqE">As a domesticated or semi-domesticated animal, the dog is nearly universal among human societies. Notable exceptions once included:</p>
<ul id="mwAqI"><li id="mwAqM">The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Aboriginal_Tasmanians" title="Aboriginal Tasmanians" id="mwAqQ">Aboriginal Tasmanians</a>, who were separated from Australia before the arrival of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dingo" title="Dingo" id="mwAqU">dingos</a> on that continent</li>
<li id="mwAqY">The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Andamanese_peoples" title="Andamanese peoples" id="mwAqc">Andamanese peoples</a>, who were isolated when <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise" id="mwAqg">rising sea levels</a> covered the land bridge to Myanmar</li>
<li id="mwAqk">The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fuegians" title="Fuegians" id="mwAqo">Fuegians</a>, who instead domesticated the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fuegian_dog" title="Fuegian dog" id="mwAqs">Fuegian dog</a>, a different canid species</li>
<li id="mwAqw">Individual Pacific islands whose maritime settlers did not bring dogs, or where dogs died out after original settlement, notably the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands" id="mwAq0">Mariana Islands</a>,<sup about="#mwt547" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-92" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-92"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-92" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 92;" id="mwAq4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAq8">[92]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Palau" title="Palau" id="mwArA">Palau</a><sup about="#mwt551" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-93" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-93"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-93" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 93;" id="mwArE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwArI">[93]</span></a></sup> and most of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands" id="mwArM">Caroline Islands</a> with exceptions such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fais_Island" title="Fais Island" id="mwArQ">Fais Island</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Nukuoro" title="Nukuoro" id="mwArU">Nukuoro</a>,<sup about="#mwt555" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-94" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-94"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-94" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 94;" id="mwArY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwArc">[94]</span></a></sup> the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands" id="mwArg">Marshall Islands</a>,<sup about="#mwt559" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Urban_95-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Urban"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Urban-95"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Urban-95" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 95;" id="mwArk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAro">[95]</span></a></sup> the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands" id="mwArs">Gilbert Islands</a>,<sup about="#mwt560" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Urban_95-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Urban"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Urban-95" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 95;" id="mwArw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAr0">[95]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia" id="mwAr4">New Caledonia</a>,<sup about="#mwt564" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Matisoo-Smith_96-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Matisoo-Smith"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Matisoo-Smith-96"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Matisoo-Smith-96" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 96;" id="mwAr8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAsA">[96]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu" id="mwAsE">Vanuatu</a>,<sup about="#mwt565" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Matisoo-Smith_96-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Matisoo-Smith"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Matisoo-Smith-96" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 96;" id="mwAsI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAsM">[96]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt569" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Forster_97-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Forster"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Forster-97"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Forster-97" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 97;" id="mwAsQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAsU">[97]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tonga" title="Tonga" id="mwAsY">Tonga</a>,<sup about="#mwt570" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Forster_97-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Forster"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Forster-97" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 97;" id="mwAsc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAsg">[97]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Marquesas" title="Marquesas" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAsk">Marquesas</a>,<sup about="#mwt571" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Forster_97-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Forster"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Forster-97" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 97;" id="mwAso"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAss">[97]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mangaia" title="Mangaia" id="mwAsw">Mangaia</a> in the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands" id="mwAs0">Cook Islands</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Rapa_Iti" title="Rapa Iti" id="mwAs4">Rapa Iti</a> in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia" id="mwAs8">French Polynesia</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Easter_Island" title="Easter Island" id="mwAtA">Easter Island</a>,<sup about="#mwt572" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Forster_97-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Forster"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Forster-97" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 97;" id="mwAtE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAtI">[97]</span></a></sup> the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Chatham_Islands" title="Chatham Islands" id="mwAtM">Chatham Islands</a><sup about="#mwt576" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-98" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-98"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-98" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 98;" id="mwAtQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAtU">[98]</span></a></sup> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pitcairn_Island" title="Pitcairn Island" id="mwAtY">Pitcairn Island</a> (settled by the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mutiny_on_the_Bounty" title="Mutiny on the Bounty" id="mwAtc"><i id="mwAtg">Bounty</i> mutineers</a>, who killed off their dogs to escape discovery by passing ships).<sup about="#mwt580" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-99" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-99"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-99" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 99;" id="mwAtk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAto">[99]</span></a></sup></li></ul>

<p id="mwAts">Dogs were introduced to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Antarctica" title="Antarctica" id="mwAtw">Antarctica</a> as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sled_dog" title="Sled dog" id="mwAt0">sled dogs</a>, but were later outlawed by international agreement due to the possible risk of spreading infections.<sup about="#mwt582" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-100" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-100"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-100" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 100;" id="mwAt4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAt8">[100]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="24" id="mwAuA"><h2 id="Roles_with_humans">Roles with humans</h2>
<p id="mwAuE">Domestic dogs inherited complex behaviors, such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bite_inhibition" title="Bite inhibition" id="mwAuI">bite inhibition</a>, from their wolf ancestors, which would have been <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pack_hunter" title="Pack hunter" id="mwAuM">pack hunters</a> with a complex body language. These sophisticated forms of social cognition and communication may account for their trainability, playfulness and ability to fit into human households and social situations. These attributes have given dogs a relationship with humans that has enabled them to become one of the most successful animals today.<sup about="#mwt587" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Miklósi_101-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Miklósi"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Miklósi-101"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Miklósi-101" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 101;" id="mwAuQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAuU">[101]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAuY">The dogs' value to early human hunter-gatherers led to them quickly becoming ubiquitous across world cultures. Dogs perform many roles for people, such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hunting_dog" title="Hunting dog" id="mwAuc">hunting</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Herding_dog" title="Herding dog" id="mwAug">herding</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sled_dog" title="Sled dog" id="mwAuk">pulling loads</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Guard_dog" title="Guard dog" id="mwAuo">protection</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Police_dog" title="Police dog" id="mwAus">assisting police</a> and the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dogs_in_warfare" title="Dogs in warfare" id="mwAuw">military</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pet" title="Pet" id="mwAu0">companionship</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Assistance_dog" title="Assistance dog" id="mwAu4">aiding disabled individuals</a>. This influence on human society has given them the nickname "<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Man's_best_friend" title="Man's best friend" id="mwAu8">man's best friend</a>" in the Western world. In some cultures, however, dogs <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dog#As_food" id="mwAvA">are also a source of meat</a>.<sup about="#mwt590" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Wingfield-Hayes_102-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Wingfield-Hayes"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Wingfield-Hayes-102" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 102;" id="mwAvE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAvI">[102]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt591" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Vietnam's_dog_meat_tradition_103-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Vietnam&apos;s dog meat tradition"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Vietnam's_dog_meat_tradition-103" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 103;" id="mwAvM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAvQ">[103]</span></a></sup></p>

<section data-mw-section-id="25" id="mwAvU"><h3 id="Pets">Pets</h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwAvY"><a href="./File:Siberian_Husky_pho.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwAvc"><img resource="./File:Siberian_Husky_pho.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Siberian_Husky_pho.jpg/220px-Siberian_Husky_pho.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="711" data-file-type="bitmap" height="209" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Siberian_Husky_pho.jpg/330px-Siberian_Husky_pho.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Siberian_Husky_pho.jpg/440px-Siberian_Husky_pho.jpg 2x" id="mwAvg"/></a><figcaption id="mwAvk"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Siberian_Husky" title="Siberian Husky" id="mwAvo">Siberian Huskies</a> are <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pack_animal" title="Pack animal" id="mwAvs">pack animals</a> that still enjoy some human companionship</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwAvw">It is estimated that three-quarters of the world's dog population lives in the developing world as feral, village, or community dogs, with pet dogs uncommon.<sup about="#mwt597" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-104" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-104"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-104" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 104;" id="mwAv0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAv4">[104]</span></a></sup><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2021" about="#mwt593" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"page needed","href":"./Template:Page_needed"},"params":{"date":{"wt":"May 2021"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAv8"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template " style="white-space:nowrap;" about="#mwt593" id="mwAwA"><span typeof="mw:Entity">[</span><i><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2021)">page<span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span>needed</span></a></i><span typeof="mw:Entity">]</span></sup></p>

<p id="mwAwE">"The most widespread form of interspecies bonding occurs between humans and dogs"<sup about="#mwt611" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Tacon_105-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Tacon"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Tacon-105"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Tacon-105" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 105;" id="mwAwI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAwM">[105]</span></a></sup> and the keeping of dogs as companions, particularly by elites, has a long history.<sup about="#mwt615" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Derr_14-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Derr"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Derr-14"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Derr-14" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 14;" id="mwAwQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAwU">[14]</span></a></sup> Pet dog populations grew significantly after <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./World_War_II" title="World War II" id="mwAwY">World War II</a> as suburbanization increased.<sup about="#mwt616" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Derr_14-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Derr"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Derr-14" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 14;" id="mwAwc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAwg">[14]</span></a></sup> In the 1950s and 1960s, dogs were kept outside more often than they tend to be today<sup about="#mwt620" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Franklin_106-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Franklin"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Franklin-106"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Franklin-106" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 106;" id="mwAwk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAwo">[106]</span></a></sup> (the expression "in the doghouse" - recorded since 1932<sup about="#mwt624" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-107" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-107"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-107" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 107;" id="mwAws"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAww">[107]</span></a></sup> - to describe exclusion from the group implies a distance between the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Doghouse" title="Doghouse" id="mwAw0">doghouse</a> and the home) and were still primarily functional, acting as a guard, children's playmate, or walking companion. From the 1980s, there have been changes in the pet dog's role, such as the increased role of dogs in the emotional support of their human guardians.<sup about="#mwt628" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Katz_108-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Katz"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Katz-108"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Katz-108" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 108;" id="mwAw4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAw8">[108]</span></a></sup><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2021" about="#mwt606" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"page needed","href":"./Template:Page_needed"},"params":{"date":{"wt":"May 2021"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAxA"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template " style="white-space:nowrap;" about="#mwt606" id="mwAxE"><span typeof="mw:Entity">[</span><i><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2021)">page<span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span>needed</span></a></i><span typeof="mw:Entity">]</span></sup> People and their dogs have become increasingly integrated and implicated in each other's lives<sup about="#mwt632" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Haraway_109-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Haraway"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Haraway-109"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Haraway-109" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 109;" id="mwAxI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAxM">[109]</span></a></sup><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2021" about="#mwt607" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"page needed","href":"./Template:Page_needed"},"params":{"date":{"wt":"May 2021"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAxQ"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template " style="white-space:nowrap;" about="#mwt607" id="mwAxU"><span typeof="mw:Entity">[</span><i><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2021)">page<span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span>needed</span></a></i><span typeof="mw:Entity">]</span></sup> to the point where pet dogs actively shape how a family and home are experienced.<sup about="#mwt636" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Power_110-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Power"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Power-110"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Power-110" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 110;" id="mwAxY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAxc">[110]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAxg">There have been two significant trends occurring within the second half of the 20th century in pet dogs' changing status. The first has been <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Commodification_of_animals" title="Commodification of animals" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAxk">"commodification"</a>, shaping it to conform to social expectations of personality and behavior.<sup about="#mwt639" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Power_110-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Power"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Power-110" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 110;" id="mwAxo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAxs">[110]</span></a></sup> The second has been the broadening of the family's concept and the home to include dogs-as-dogs within everyday routines and practices.<sup about="#mwt640" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Power_110-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Power"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Power-110" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 110;" id="mwAxw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAx0">[110]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAx4">A vast range of commodity forms aims to transform a pet dog into an ideal companion.<sup about="#mwt647" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Nast_111-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Nast"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Nast-111"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Nast-111" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 111;" id="mwAx8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAyA">[111]</span></a></sup> The list of goods, services, and places available is enormous: from dog perfumes, couture, furniture and housing to dog groomers, therapists, trainers and caretakers, dog cafes, spas, parks and beaches and dog hotels, airlines and cemeteries.<sup about="#mwt648" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Nast_111-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Nast"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Nast-111" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 111;" id="mwAyE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAyI">[111]</span></a></sup> Dog training books, classes, and television programs proliferated as the process of commodifying the pet dog continued.<sup about="#mwt652" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Myths_112-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Myths"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Myths-112"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Myths-112" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 112;" id="mwAyM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAyQ">[112]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAyU">The majority of contemporary dog owners describe their pet as part of the family, although some ambivalence about the relationship is evident in the popular reconceptualization of the dog-human family as a pack.<sup about="#mwt658" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Power_110-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Power"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Power-110" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 110;" id="mwAyY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAyc">[110]</span></a></sup> Some dog trainers, such as on the television program <i id="mwAyg"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dog_Whisperer" title="Dog Whisperer" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAyk">Dog Whisperer</a></i>, have promoted a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dominance_(ethology)" title="Dominance (ethology)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAyo">dominance model</a> of dog-human relationships. However, it has been disputed that "trying to achieve status" is characteristic of dog-human interactions.<sup about="#mwt662" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Bradshaw_113-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Bradshaw"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Bradshaw-113"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Bradshaw-113" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 113;" id="mwAys"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAyw">[113]</span></a></sup> The idea of the "<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pack_(canine)#Use_in_dog_training" title="Pack (canine)" id="mwAy0">alpha dog</a>" trying to be dominant is based on a disproved theory about wolf packs.<sup about="#mwt666" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-114" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-114"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-114" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 114;" id="mwAy4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAy8">[114]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt670" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-115" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-115"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-115" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 115;" id="mwAzA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAzE">[115]</span></a></sup> Pet dogs play an active role in family life; for example, a study of conversations in dog-human families showed how family members use the dog as a resource, talking to the dog, or talking through the dog; to mediate their interactions with each other.<sup about="#mwt674" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Tannen_116-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Tannen"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Tannen-116"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Tannen-116" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 116;" id="mwAzI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAzM">[116]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAzQ">Increasingly, human family-members engage in activities centered on the dog's perceived needs and interests, or in which the dog is an integral partner, such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Musical_canine_freestyle" title="Musical canine freestyle" id="mwAzU">dog dancing</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Doga_(Dog_Yoga)" title="Doga (Dog Yoga)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAzY">dog yoga</a>.<sup about="#mwt676" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Nast_111-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Nast"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Nast-111" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 111;" id="mwAzc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAzg">[111]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAzk">According to statistics published by the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./American_Pet_Products_Manufacturers_Association" title="American Pet Products Manufacturers Association" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAzo">American Pet Products Manufacturers Association</a> in the National Pet Owner Survey in 2009–2010, an estimated 77.5<span typeof="mw:Entity" id="mwAzs"> </span>million people in the United States have pet dogs.<sup about="#mwt682" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-HSO_117-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"HSO"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-HSO-117"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-HSO-117" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 117;" id="mwAzw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAz0">[117]</span></a></sup> The same source shows that nearly 40% of American households own at least one dog, of which 67% own just one dog, 25% two dogs and nearly 9% more than two dogs. There does not seem to be any <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Gender_preference_(disambiguation)" title="Gender preference (disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" id="mwAz4">gender preference</a> among dogs as pets, as the statistical data reveal an equal number of male and female pet dogs. Although several programs promote <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pet_adoption" title="Pet adoption" id="mwAz8">pet adoption</a>, less than one-fifth of the owned dogs come from <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Animal_shelter" title="Animal shelter" id="mwA0A">shelters</a>.<sup about="#mwt683" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-HSO_117-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"HSO"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-HSO-117" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 117;" id="mwA0E"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA0I">[117]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA0M">A study using <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Magnetic_resonance_imaging" title="Magnetic resonance imaging" id="mwA0Q">magnetic resonance imaging</a> (MRI) to compare humans and dogs showed that dogs have the same response to voices and use the same parts of the brain as humans do. This gives dogs the ability to recognize human emotional sounds, making them friendly social pets to humans.<sup about="#mwt685" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Andics2014_118-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Andics2014"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Andics2014-118" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 118;" id="mwA0U"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA0Y">[118]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="26" id="mwA0c"><h3 id="Workers">Workers</h3>
<p id="mwA0g">Dogs have lived and worked with humans in many roles. In addition to dogs' role as companion animals, dogs have been bred for herding livestock (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Collie" title="Collie" id="mwA0k">collies</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sheepdog" title="Sheepdog" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA0o">sheepdogs</a>),<sup about="#mwt701" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-119" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-119"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-119" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 119;" id="mwA0s"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA0w">[119]</span></a></sup><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2021" about="#mwt696" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"page needed","href":"./Template:Page_needed"},"params":{"date":{"wt":"May 2021"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwA00"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template " style="white-space:nowrap;" about="#mwt696" id="mwA04"><span typeof="mw:Entity">[</span><i><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2021)">page<span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span>needed</span></a></i><span typeof="mw:Entity">]</span></sup><sup about="#mwt702" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-ADW_12-4" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"ADW"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-ADW-12"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-ADW-12" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 12;" id="mwA08"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA1A">[12]</span></a></sup>  hunting (hounds, pointers)<sup about="#mwt706" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-serpell1995_120-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"serpell1995"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-serpell1995-120"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-serpell1995-120" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 120;" id="mwA1E"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA1I">[120]</span></a></sup><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2021" about="#mwt697" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"page needed","href":"./Template:Page_needed"},"params":{"date":{"wt":"May 2021"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwA1M"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template " style="white-space:nowrap;" about="#mwt697" id="mwA1Q"><span typeof="mw:Entity">[</span><i><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2021)">page<span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span>needed</span></a></i><span typeof="mw:Entity">]</span></sup> and rodent control (terriers).<sup about="#mwt707" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-ADW_12-5" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"ADW"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-ADW-12" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 12;" id="mwA1U"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA1Y">[12]</span></a></sup> Other types of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Working_dog" title="Working dog" id="mwA1c">working dogs</a> include <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Search_and_rescue_dog" title="Search and rescue dog" id="mwA1g">search and rescue dogs</a>,<sup about="#mwt708" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-121" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-121"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-121" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 121;" id="mwA1k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA1o">[121]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Detection_dog" title="Detection dog" id="mwA1s">detection dogs</a> trained to detect <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade" id="mwA1w">illicit drugs</a><sup about="#mwt709" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-122" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-122"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-122" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 122;" id="mwA10"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA14">[122]</span></a></sup> or <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Chemical_weapon" title="Chemical weapon" id="mwA18">chemical weapons</a>;<sup about="#mwt710" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-123" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-123"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-123" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 123;" id="mwA2A"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA2E">[123]</span></a></sup> guard dogs; dogs who assist fishermen with the use of nets; and dogs that pull loads.<sup about="#mwt711" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-ADW_12-6" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"ADW"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-ADW-12" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 12;" id="mwA2I"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA2M">[12]</span></a></sup> In 1957, the dog <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Laika" title="Laika" id="mwA2Q">Laika</a> became the first animal to be launched into <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Earth_orbit" title="Earth orbit" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA2U">Earth orbit</a>, aboard the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Soviet_space_program" title="Soviet space program" id="mwA2Y">Soviets</a>' <i id="mwA2c"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sputnik_2" title="Sputnik 2" id="mwA2g">Sputnik 2</a></i>; she died during the flight.<sup about="#mwt715" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-124" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-124"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-124" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 124;" id="mwA2k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA2o">[124]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt719" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-125" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-125"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-125" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 125;" id="mwA2s"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA2w">[125]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA20">Various kinds of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Service_dog" title="Service dog" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA24">service dogs</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Assistance_dog" title="Assistance dog" id="mwA28">assistance dogs</a>, including <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Guide_dog" title="Guide dog" id="mwA3A">guide dogs</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hearing_dog" title="Hearing dog" id="mwA3E">hearing dogs</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mobility_assistance_dog" title="Mobility assistance dog" id="mwA3I">mobility assistance dogs</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Psychiatric_service_dog" title="Psychiatric service dog" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA3M">psychiatric service dogs</a>, assist individuals with disabilities.<sup about="#mwt726" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-126" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-126"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-126" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 126;" id="mwA3Q"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA3U">[126]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt730" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-127" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-127"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-127" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 127;" id="mwA3Y"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA3c">[127]</span></a></sup> Some dogs owned by people with epilepsy have been shown to alert their handler when the handler shows signs of an impending seizure, sometimes well in advance of onset, allowing the guardian to seek safety, medication, or medical care.<sup about="#mwt734" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-seizure_128-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"seizure"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-seizure-128"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-seizure-128" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 128;" id="mwA3g"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA3k">[128]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="27" id="mwA3o"><h3 id="Athletes_and_models">Athletes and models</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt735" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"See also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Conformation show"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwA3s"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt735" id="mwA3w">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Conformation_show" title="Conformation show" class="mw-redirect">Conformation show</a></div>

<p id="mwA30">People often enter their dogs in competitions, such as breed-conformation shows or <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./List_of_dog_sports" title="List of dog sports" id="mwA34">sports</a>, including racing, sledding and agility competitions. In conformation shows, also referred to as breed shows, a judge familiar with the specific dog breed evaluates individual purebred dogs for conformity with their established breed type as described in the breed standard. As the breed standard only deals with the dog's externally observable qualities (such as appearance, movement and temperament), separately tested qualities (such as ability or health) are not part of the judging in conformation shows.</p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="28" id="mwA38"><h3 id="Food">Food</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt738" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Dog meat"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwA4A"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt738" id="mwA4E">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dog_meat" title="Dog meat">Dog meat</a></div>
<p id="mwA4I">Dog meat is consumed in some <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./East_Asian" title="East Asian" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA4M">East Asian</a> countries, including <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Korea" title="Korea" id="mwA4Q">Korea</a>,<sup about="#mwt762" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-129" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-129"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-129" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 129;" id="mwA4U"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA4Y">[129]</span></a></sup><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2021" about="#mwt757" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"page needed","href":"./Template:Page_needed"},"params":{"date":{"wt":"May 2021"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwA4c"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template " style="white-space:nowrap;" about="#mwt757" id="mwA4g"><span typeof="mw:Entity">[</span><i><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2021)">page<span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span>needed</span></a></i><span typeof="mw:Entity">]</span></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./China" title="China" id="mwA4k">China</a>,<sup about="#mwt766" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Wingfield-Hayes_102-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Wingfield-Hayes"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Wingfield-Hayes-102"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Wingfield-Hayes-102" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 102;" id="mwA4o"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA4s">[102]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vietnam" title="Vietnam" id="mwA4w">Vietnam</a><sup about="#mwt770" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Vietnam's_dog_meat_tradition_103-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Vietnam&apos;s dog meat tradition"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Vietnam&apos;s_dog_meat_tradition-103"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Vietnam's_dog_meat_tradition-103" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 103;" id="mwA40"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA44">[103]</span></a></sup> and the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Philippines" title="Philippines" id="mwA48">Philippines</a>,<sup about="#mwt774" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-130" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-130"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-130" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 130;" id="mwA5A"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5E">[130]</span></a></sup> which dates back to antiquity.<sup about="#mwt778" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-131" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-131"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-131" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 131;" id="mwA5I"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5M">[131]</span></a></sup> Based on limited data, it is estimated that 13–16<span typeof="mw:Entity" id="mwA5Q"> </span>million dogs are killed and consumed in Asia every year.<sup about="#mwt782" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-132" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-132"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-132" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 132;" id="mwA5U"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5Y">[132]</span></a></sup> In China, debates have ensued over banning the consumption of dog meat.<sup about="#mwt786" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-133" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-133"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-133" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 133;" id="mwA5c"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5g">[133]</span></a></sup>  Following the Sui and Tang dynasties of the first millennium, however, people living on northern China's plains began to eschew eating dogs, which is likely due to Buddhism and Islam's spread, two religions that forbade the consumption of certain animals, including the dog. As members of the upper classes shunned dog meat, it gradually became a social taboo to eat it, even though the general population continued to consume it for centuries afterward.<link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:All_articles_with_unsourced_statements" about="#mwt758" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Cn","href":"./Template:Cn"},"params":{"date":{"wt":"September 2022"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwA5k"/><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Articles_with_unsourced_statements_from_September_2022" about="#mwt758"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;" about="#mwt758" id="mwA5o"><span typeof="mw:Entity">[</span><i><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i><span typeof="mw:Entity">]</span></sup> Dog meat is also consumed in some parts of Switzerland.<sup about="#mwt790" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-134" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-134"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-134" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 134;" id="mwA5s"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5w">[134]</span></a></sup> Other cultures, such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Polynesia" title="Polynesia" id="mwA50">Polynesia</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pre-Columbian_Mexico" title="Pre-Columbian Mexico" id="mwA54">pre-Columbian Mexico</a>, also consumed dog meat in their history. Dog fat is also reportedly believed to be beneficial for the lungs in some parts of Poland<sup about="#mwt794" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-135" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-135"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-135" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 135;" id="mwA58"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6A">[135]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt799" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-136" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-136"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-136" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 136;" id="mwA6E"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6I">[136]</span></a></sup> and Central Asia.<sup about="#mwt803" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-:2_137-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":":2"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-:2-137"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-:2-137" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 137;" id="mwA6M"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6Q">[137]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt807" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-138" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-138"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-138" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 138;" id="mwA6U"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6Y">[138]</span></a></sup> Proponents of eating dog meat have argued that placing a distinction between livestock and dogs is Western hypocrisy and that there is no difference in eating different animals' meat.<sup about="#mwt811" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-139" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-139"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-139" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 139;" id="mwA6c"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6g">[139]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt815" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-140" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-140"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-140" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 140;" id="mwA6k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6o">[140]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt819" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-141" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-141"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-141" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 141;" id="mwA6s"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6w">[141]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt823" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-142" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-142"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-142" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 142;" id="mwA60"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA64">[142]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA68">In Korea, the primary dog breed raised for meat, the <i id="mwA7A"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Nureongi" title="Nureongi" id="mwA7E">Nureongi</a></i>, differs from those breeds raised for pets that Koreans may keep in their homes.<sup about="#mwt828" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-pettid_143-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"pettid"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-pettid-143"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-pettid-143" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 143;" id="mwA7I"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA7M">[143]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA7Q">The most popular Korean dog dish is called <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bosintang" title="Bosintang" id="mwA7U">bosintang</a>, a spicy stew meant to balance the body's heat during the summer months. Followers of the custom claim this is done to ensure good health by balancing one's <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Qi" title="Qi" id="mwA7Y"><i id="mwA7c">gi</i></a>, or the body's vital energy. A 19th-century version of bosintang explains that the dish is prepared by boiling dog meat with <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Scallion" title="Scallion" id="mwA7g">scallions</a> and chili powder. Variations of the dish contain chicken and bamboo shoots. While the dishes are still prevalent in Korea with a segment of the population, dog is not as widely consumed as beef, pork and chicken.<sup about="#mwt830" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-pettid_143-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"pettid"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-pettid-143" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 143;" id="mwA7k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA7o">[143]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="29" id="mwA7s"><h3 id="Health_risks">Health risks</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt831" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Further","href":"./Template:Further"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Dog bite"},"2":{"wt":"Canine vector-borne disease"},"3":{"wt":"Dog bite prevention"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwA7w"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt831" id="mwA70">Further information: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dog_bite" title="Dog bite">Dog bite</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Canine_vector-borne_disease" title="Canine vector-borne disease">Canine vector-borne disease</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dog_bite_prevention" title="Dog bite prevention" class="mw-redirect">Dog bite prevention</a></div>

<p id="mwA74">In 2018, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./WHO" title="WHO" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA78">WHO</a> reported that 59,000 people died globally from <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Rabies" title="Rabies" id="mwA8A">rabies</a>, with 59.6% in Asia and 36.4% in Africa. Rabies is a disease for which dogs are the most important vector.<sup about="#mwt840" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-144" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-144"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-144" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 144;" id="mwA8E"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA8I">[144]</span></a></sup> Significant dog bites affect tens of millions of people globally each year. Children in mid-to-late childhood are the largest percentage bitten by dogs, with a greater risk of injury to the head and neck.
