They are more likely to need medical treatment and have the highest death rate.<sup about="#mwt844" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-145" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-145"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-145" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 145;" id="mwA8M"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA8Q">[145]</span></a></sup> Sharp claws with powerful muscles behind them can lacerate flesh in a scratch that can lead to serious infections.<sup about="#mwt848" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-146" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-146"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-146" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 146;" id="mwA8U"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA8Y">[146]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA8c">In the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dogs_in_the_United_States" title="Dogs in the United States" id="mwA8g">U.S.</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cat" title="Cat" id="mwA8k">cats</a> and dogs are a factor in more than 86,000 falls each year.<sup about="#mwt854" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-147" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-147"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-147" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 147;" id="mwA8o"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA8s">[147]</span></a></sup> It has been estimated that around 2% of dog-related injuries treated in U.K. hospitals are domestic accidents. The same study found that while dog involvement in road traffic accidents was difficult to quantify, dog-associated road accidents involving injury more commonly involved two-wheeled vehicles.<sup about="#mwt858" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-148" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-148"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-148" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 148;" id="mwA8w"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA80">[148]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA84"><i id="mwA88"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Toxocara_canis" title="Toxocara canis" id="mwA9A">Toxocara canis</a></i> (dog <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Roundworm" title="Roundworm" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA9E">roundworm</a>) eggs in dog feces can cause <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Toxocariasis" title="Toxocariasis" id="mwA9I">toxocariasis</a>. In the United States, about 10,000 cases of <i id="mwA9M">Toxocara</i> infection are reported in humans each year, and almost 14% of the U.S. population is infected.<sup about="#mwt866" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-149" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-149"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-149" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 149;" id="mwA9Q"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA9U">[149]</span></a></sup> Untreated toxocariasis can cause retinal damage and decreased vision.<sup about="#mwt870" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-kidshealth_150-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"kidshealth"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-kidshealth-150"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-kidshealth-150" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 150;" id="mwA9Y"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA9c">[150]</span></a></sup> Dog feces can also contain <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hookworm" title="Hookworm" id="mwA9g">hookworms</a> that cause <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cutaneous_larva_migrans" title="Cutaneous larva migrans" id="mwA9k">cutaneous larva migrans</a> in humans.<sup about="#mwt874" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-151" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-151"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-151" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 151;" id="mwA9o"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA9s">[151]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt878" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-152" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-152"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-152" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 152;" id="mwA9w"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA90">[152]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="30" id="mwA94"><h3 id="Health_benefits">Health benefits</h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwA98"><a href="./File:Walking_the_dog_(1945527533).jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwA-A"><img resource="./File:Walking_the_dog_(1945527533).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Walking_the_dog_%281945527533%29.jpg/220px-Walking_the_dog_%281945527533%29.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" data-file-type="bitmap" height="330" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Walking_the_dog_%281945527533%29.jpg/330px-Walking_the_dog_%281945527533%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Walking_the_dog_%281945527533%29.jpg/440px-Walking_the_dog_%281945527533%29.jpg 2x" id="mwA-E"/></a><figcaption id="mwA-I">Walking a dog</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwA-M">Dogs suffer from the same common disorders as humans; these include cancer, diabetes, heart disease and neurologic disorders. Their pathology is similar to humans, as is their response to treatment and their outcomes. Researchers are identifying the genes associated with dog diseases similar to human disorders, but lack mouse models to find cures for both dogs and humans. The genes involved in canine obsessive-compulsive disorders led to the detection of four genes in humans' related pathways.<sup about="#mwt880" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Ostrander2019_10-6" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Ostrander2019"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Ostrander2019-10" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 10;" id="mwA-Q"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA-U">[10]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA-Y">The scientific evidence is mixed as to whether a dog's companionship can enhance human physical health and psychological well-being.<sup about="#mwt888" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Pet_ownership_and_human_health:_a_brief_review_of_evidence_and_issues_153-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Pet ownership and human health: a brief review of evidence and issues"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Pet_ownership_and_human_health:_a_brief_review_of_evidence_and_issues-153"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Pet_ownership_and_human_health:_a_brief_review_of_evidence_and_issues-153" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 153;" id="mwA-c"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA-g">[153]</span></a></sup> Studies suggesting that there are benefits to physical health and psychological well-being<sup about="#mwt892" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-154" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-154"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-154" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 154;" id="mwA-k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA-o">[154]</span></a></sup> have been criticized for being poorly controlled.<sup about="#mwt896" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Health_effects_of_ownership_of_and_attachment_to_companion_animals_in_an_older_population_155-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Health effects of ownership of and attachment to companion animals in an older population"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Health_effects_of_ownership_of_and_attachment_to_companion_animals_in_an_older_population-155"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Health_effects_of_ownership_of_and_attachment_to_companion_animals_in_an_older_population-155" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 155;" id="mwA-s"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA-w">[155]</span></a></sup> It found that "the health of elderly people is related to their health habits and social supports but not to their ownership of, or attachment to, a companion animal." Earlier studies have shown that people who keep pet dogs or cats exhibit better mental and physical health than those who do not, making fewer visits to the doctor and being less likely to be on medication than non-guardians.<sup about="#mwt900" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-156" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-156"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-156" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 156;" id="mwA-0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA-4">[156]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA-8">A 2005 paper states "recent research has failed to support earlier findings that pet ownership is associated with a reduced risk of cardiovascular disease, a reduced use of general practitioner services, or any psychological or physical benefits on health for community dwelling older people. Research has, however, pointed to significantly less absenteeism from school through sickness among children who live with pets."<sup about="#mwt903" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Pet_ownership_and_human_health:_a_brief_review_of_evidence_and_issues_153-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Pet ownership and human health: a brief review of evidence and issues"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Pet_ownership_and_human_health:_a_brief_review_of_evidence_and_issues-153" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 153;" id="mwA_A"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA_E">[153]</span></a></sup> In one study, new guardians reported a highly significant reduction in minor health problems during the first month following pet acquisition. This effect was sustained in those with dogs through to the end of the study.<sup about="#mwt907" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated717_157-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"autogenerated717"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-autogenerated717-157"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-autogenerated717-157" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 157;" id="mwA_I"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA_M">[157]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA_Q">People with pet dogs took considerably more physical exercise than those with cats and those without pets. The results provide evidence that keeping pets may have positive effects on human health and behavior and that for guardians of dogs, these effects are relatively long-term.<sup about="#mwt911" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated717_157-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"autogenerated717"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-autogenerated717-157" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 157;" id="mwA_U"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA_Y">[157]</span></a></sup> Pet guardianship has also been associated with increased coronary artery disease survival. Human guardians are significantly less likely to die within one year of an acute myocardial infarction than those who did not own dogs.<sup about="#mwt915" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-158" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-158"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-158" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 158;" id="mwA_c"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA_g">[158]</span></a></sup> The association between dog ownership and adult physical activity levels has been reviewed by several authors.<sup about="#mwt919" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-159" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-159"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-159" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 159;" id="mwA_k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA_o">[159]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA_s">The health benefits of dogs can result from contact with dogs in general, not solely from having dogs as pets. For example, when in a pet dog's presence, people show reductions in cardiovascular, behavioral and psychological indicators of anxiety.<sup about="#mwt927" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-160" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-160"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-160" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 160;" id="mwA_w"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA_0">[160]</span></a></sup> Other health benefits are gained from exposure to immune-stimulating microorganisms, which can protect against allergies and autoimmune diseases according to the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hygiene_hypothesis" title="Hygiene hypothesis" id="mwA_4">hygiene hypothesis</a>. The benefits of contact with a dog also include social support, as dogs cannot only provide companionship and social support themselves but also act as facilitators of social interactions between humans.<sup about="#mwt931" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-161" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-161"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-161" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 161;" id="mwA_8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBAA">[161]</span></a></sup> One study indicated that wheelchair users experience more positive social interactions with strangers when accompanied by a dog than when they are not.<sup about="#mwt935" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-162" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-162"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-162" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 162;" id="mwBAE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBAI">[162]</span></a></sup> In 2015, a study found that pet owners were significantly more likely to get to know people in their neighborhood than non-pet owners.<sup about="#mwt939" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-163" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-163"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-163" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 163;" id="mwBAM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBAQ">[163]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBAU">Using dogs and other animals as a part of therapy dates back to the late 18th century, when animals were introduced into mental institutions to help socialize patients with mental disorders.<sup about="#mwt946" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-164" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-164"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-164" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 164;" id="mwBAY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBAc">[164]</span></a></sup> Animal-assisted intervention research has shown that animal-assisted therapy with a dog can increase social behaviors, such as smiling and laughing, among people with Alzheimer's disease.<sup about="#mwt950" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-165" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-165"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-165" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 165;" id="mwBAg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBAk">[165]</span></a></sup> One study demonstrated that children with ADHD and conduct disorders who participated in an education program with dogs and other animals showed increased attendance, increased knowledge and skill objectives and decreased antisocial and violent behavior compared with those not in an animal-assisted program.<sup about="#mwt954" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-166" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-166"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-166" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 166;" id="mwBAo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBAs">[166]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="31" id="mwBAw"><h3 id="Cultural_importance">Cultural importance</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt955" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Cultural depictions of dogs"},"2":{"wt":"Dogs in religion"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBA0"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt955" id="mwBA4">Main articles: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cultural_depictions_of_dogs" title="Cultural depictions of dogs">Cultural depictions of dogs</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dogs_in_religion" title="Dogs in religion">Dogs in religion</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt958" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"further","href":"./Template:Further"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"List of fictional dogs"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBA8"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt958" id="mwBBA">Further information: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./List_of_fictional_dogs" title="List of fictional dogs">List of fictional dogs</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBBE"><a href="./File:Cerberus-Blake.jpeg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBBI"><img resource="./File:Cerberus-Blake.jpeg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Cerberus-Blake.jpeg/220px-Cerberus-Blake.jpeg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="725" data-file-type="bitmap" height="156" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Cerberus-Blake.jpeg/330px-Cerberus-Blake.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Cerberus-Blake.jpeg/440px-Cerberus-Blake.jpeg 2x" id="mwBBM"/></a><figcaption id="mwBBQ"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cerberus" title="Cerberus" id="mwBBU">Cerberus</a>, with the gluttons in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dante" title="Dante" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBBY">Dante</a>'s <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Third_Circle_of_Hell" title="Third Circle of Hell" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBBc">Third Circle of Hell</a>. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./William_Blake" title="William Blake" id="mwBBg">William Blake</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p id="mwBBk">Dogs were depicted to symbolize <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Guide" title="Guide" id="mwBBo">guidance</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Protection" title="Protection" id="mwBBs">protection</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Loyalty" title="Loyalty" id="mwBBw">loyalty</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fidelity" title="Fidelity" id="mwBB0">fidelity</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Faithfulness" title="Faithfulness" id="mwBB4">faithfulness</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Alertness" title="Alertness" id="mwBB8">alertness</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Love" title="Love" id="mwBCA">love</a>.<sup about="#mwt969" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-167" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-167"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-167" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 167;" id="mwBCE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBCI">[167]</span></a></sup> In ancient <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia" id="mwBCM">Mesopotamia</a>, from the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Babylonia" title="Babylonia" id="mwBCQ">Old Babylonian period</a> until the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Neo-Babylonian_Empire" title="Neo-Babylonian Empire" id="mwBCU">Neo-Babylonian</a>, dogs were the symbol of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ninisina" title="Ninisina" id="mwBCY">Ninisina</a>, the goddess of healing and medicine,<sup about="#mwt973" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-BlackGreen1992_168-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"BlackGreen1992"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-BlackGreen1992-168"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-168" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 168;" id="mwBCc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBCg">[168]</span></a></sup> and her worshippers frequently dedicated small models of seated dogs to her.<sup about="#mwt974" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-BlackGreen1992_168-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"BlackGreen1992"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-168" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 168;" id="mwBCk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBCo">[168]</span></a></sup> In the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Neo-Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo-Assyrian Empire" id="mwBCs">Neo-Assyrian</a> and Neo-Babylonian periods, dogs were used as emblems of magical protection.<sup about="#mwt975" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-BlackGreen1992_168-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"BlackGreen1992"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-168" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 168;" id="mwBCw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBC0">[168]</span></a></sup> In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./China" title="China" id="mwBC4">China</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Korea" title="Korea" id="mwBC8">Korea</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Japan" title="Japan" id="mwBDA">Japan</a>, dogs are viewed as kind protectors.<sup about="#mwt976" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherman2008_169-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherman2008"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Sherman2008-169" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 169;" id="mwBDE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDI">[169]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBDM">In mythology, dogs often serve as pets or as watchdogs.<sup about="#mwt992" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherman2008_169-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherman2008"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Sherman2008-169"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Sherman2008-169" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 169;" id="mwBDQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDU">[169]</span></a></sup> Stories of dogs guarding the gates of the underworld recur throughout Indo-European mythologies<sup about="#mwt996" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-MalloryAdams2006_170-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"MalloryAdams2006"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-MalloryAdams2006-170"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-MalloryAdams2006-170" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 170;" id="mwBDY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDc">[170]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt1000" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-West2007_171-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"West2007"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-West2007-171"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-West2007-171" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 171;" id="mwBDg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDk">[171]</span></a></sup> and may originate from <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Proto-Indo-European_religion" title="Proto-Indo-European religion" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBDo">Proto-Indo-European religion</a>.<sup about="#mwt1001" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-MalloryAdams2006_170-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"MalloryAdams2006"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-MalloryAdams2006-170" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 170;" id="mwBDs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDw">[170]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt1002" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-West2007_171-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"West2007"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-West2007-171" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 171;" id="mwBD0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBD4">[171]</span></a></sup> In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology" id="mwBD8">Greek mythology</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cerberus" title="Cerberus" id="mwBEA">Cerberus</a> is a three-headed, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dragon" title="Dragon" id="mwBEE">dragon</a>-tailed watchdog who guards the gates of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hades" title="Hades" id="mwBEI">Hades</a>.<sup about="#mwt1003" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherman2008_169-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherman2008"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Sherman2008-169" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 169;" id="mwBEM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBEQ">[169]</span></a></sup> Dogs are also associated with the Greek goddess <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hecate" title="Hecate" id="mwBEU">Hecate</a>.<sup about="#mwt1007" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-172" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-172"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-172" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 172;" id="mwBEY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBEc">[172]</span></a></sup> In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Norse_mythology" title="Norse mythology" id="mwBEg">Norse mythology</a>, a bloody, four-eyed dog called <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Garmr" title="Garmr" id="mwBEk">Garmr</a> guards <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Helheim" title="Helheim" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBEo">Helheim</a>.<sup about="#mwt1008" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherman2008_169-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherman2008"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Sherman2008-169" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 169;" id="mwBEs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBEw">[169]</span></a></sup> In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Persian_mythology" title="Persian mythology" id="mwBE0">Persian mythology</a>, two four-eyed dogs guard the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Chinvat_Bridge" title="Chinvat Bridge" id="mwBE4">Chinvat Bridge</a>.<sup about="#mwt1009" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherman2008_169-4" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherman2008"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Sherman2008-169" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 169;" id="mwBE8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBFA">[169]</span></a></sup> In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Welsh_mythology" title="Welsh mythology" id="mwBFE">Welsh mythology</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Annwn" title="Annwn" id="mwBFI">Annwn</a> is guarded by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cŵn_Annwn" title="Cŵn Annwn" id="mwBFM">Cŵn Annwn</a>.<sup about="#mwt1010" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherman2008_169-5" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherman2008"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Sherman2008-169" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 169;" id="mwBFQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBFU">[169]</span></a></sup> In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hindu_mythology" title="Hindu mythology" id="mwBFY">Hindu mythology</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Yama" title="Yama" id="mwBFc">Yama</a>, the god of death, owns two watchdogs who have four eyes. They are said to watch over the gates of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Naraka" title="Naraka" id="mwBFg">Naraka</a>.<sup about="#mwt1014" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-173" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-173"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-173" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 173;" id="mwBFk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBFo">[173]</span></a></sup> A black dog is also considered to be the <i id="mwBFs"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vahana" title="Vahana" id="mwBFw">vahana</a></i> (vehicle) of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bhairava" title="Bhairava" id="mwBF0">Bhairava</a> (an incarnation of Shiva).<sup about="#mwt1018" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-174" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-174"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-174" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 174;" id="mwBF4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBF8">[174]</span></a></sup></p> 

<p id="mwBGA">In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Christianity" title="Christianity" id="mwBGE">Christianity</a>, dogs represent faithfulness.<sup about="#mwt1027" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherman2008_169-6" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherman2008"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Sherman2008-169" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 169;" id="mwBGI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBGM">[169]</span></a></sup> Within the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBGQ">Roman Catholic</a> denomination specifically, the iconography of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Saint_Dominic" title="Saint Dominic" id="mwBGU">Saint Dominic</a> includes a dog, after the saint's mother dreamt of a dog springing from her womb and becoming pregnant shortly after that.<sup about="#mwt1031" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-CP2017_175-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"CP2017"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-CP2017-175"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-CP2017-175" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 175;" id="mwBGY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBGc">[175]</span></a></sup> As such, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order" id="mwBGg">Dominican Order</a> (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ecclesiastical_Latin" title="Ecclesiastical Latin" id="mwBGk">Ecclesiastical Latin</a>: <i id="mwBGo">Domini canis</i>) means "dog of the Lord" or "hound of the Lord" (Ecclesiastical Latin: <i id="mwBGs">Domini canis</i>).<sup about="#mwt1032" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-CP2017_175-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"CP2017"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-CP2017-175" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 175;" id="mwBGw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBG0">[175]</span></a></sup> In Christian folklore, a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Church_grim" title="Church grim" id="mwBG4">church grim</a> often takes the form of a black dog to guard Christian churches and their <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Churchyard" title="Churchyard" id="mwBG8">churchyards</a> from <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sacrilege" title="Sacrilege" id="mwBHA">sacrilege</a>.<sup about="#mwt1036" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Dyer1898_176-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Dyer1898"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Dyer1898-176"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Dyer1898-176" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 176;" id="mwBHE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBHI">[176]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Jewish_law" title="Jewish law" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBHM">Jewish law</a> does not prohibit keeping dogs and other pets. Jewish law requires Jews to feed dogs (and other animals that they own) before themselves and make arrangements for feeding them before obtaining them.<link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:All_articles_with_unsourced_statements" about="#mwt1026" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Cn","href":"./Template:Cn"},"params":{"date":{"wt":"September 2022"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBHQ"/><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Articles_with_unsourced_statements_from_September_2022" about="#mwt1026"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;" about="#mwt1026" id="mwBHU"><span typeof="mw:Entity">[</span><i><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i><span typeof="mw:Entity">]</span></sup> The view on dogs in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Islam" title="Islam" id="mwBHY">Islam</a> is mixed, with some schools of thought viewing it as unclean,<sup about="#mwt1037" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherman2008_169-7" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherman2008"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Sherman2008-169" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 169;" id="mwBHc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBHg">[169]</span></a></sup> although <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Khaled_Abou_El_Fadl" title="Khaled Abou El Fadl" id="mwBHk">Khaled Abou El Fadl</a> states that this view is based on "pre-Islamic Arab mythology" and "a tradition to be falsely attributed to the Prophet."<sup about="#mwt1041" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-177" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-177"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-177" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 177;" id="mwBHo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBHs">[177]</span></a></sup> Therefore, Sunni Malaki and Hanafi jurists permit the trade of and keeping of dogs as pets.<sup about="#mwt1045" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-178" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-178"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-178" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 178;" id="mwBHw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBH0">[178]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="32" id="mwBH4"><h2 id="Terminology">Terminology</h2>
<ul id="mwBH8"><li id="mwBIA"><i id="mwBIE">Dog</i> – the species (or subspecies) as a whole, also any male member of the same.<sup about="#mwt1046" class="mw-ref reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarperCollins2021[httpswwwcollinsdictionarycomdictionaryenglishdog_"dog"]_179-0' rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfnp","href":"./Template:Sfnp"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"HarperCollins"},"2":{"wt":"2021"},"loc":{"wt":"[https://www.collinsdictionary.com/dictionary/english/dog \"dog\"]"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href='./Dog#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarperCollins2021[httpswwwcollinsdictionarycomdictionaryenglishdog_"dog"]-179' style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 179;" id="mwBII"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBIM">[179]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mwBIQ"><i id="mwBIU">Bitch</i> – any female member of the species (or subspecies).<sup about="#mwt1049" class="mw-ref reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarperCollins2021[httpswwwcollinsdictionarycomdictionaryenglishbitch_"bitch"]_180-0' rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfnp","href":"./Template:Sfnp"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"HarperCollins"},"2":{"wt":"2021"},"loc":{"wt":"[https://www.collinsdictionary.com/dictionary/english/bitch \"bitch\"]"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href='./Dog#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarperCollins2021[httpswwwcollinsdictionarycomdictionaryenglishbitch_"bitch"]-180' style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 180;" id="mwBIY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBIc">[180]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mwBIg"><i id="mwBIk"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Puppy" title="Puppy" id="mwBIo">Puppy</a></i> or <i id="mwBIs">pup</i> – a young member of the species (or subspecies) under 12 months old.<sup about="#mwt1056" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Alderton_181-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Alderton"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Alderton-181"}}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Alderton-181" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 181;" id="mwBIw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBI0">[181]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mwBI4"><i id="mwBI8">Sire</i> – the male parent of a litter.<sup about="#mwt1057" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Alderton_181-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"r","href":"./Template:R"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Alderton"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Alderton-181" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 181;" id="mwBJA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBJE">[181]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mwBJI"><i id="mwBJM">Dam</i> – the female parent of a litter.<sup about="#mwt1060" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Alderton_181-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"r","href":"./Template:R"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Alderton"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Alderton-181" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 181;" id="mwBJQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBJU">[181]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mwBJY"><i id="mwBJc"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Litter_(animal)" title="Litter (animal)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBJg">Litter</a></i> – all of the puppies resulting from a single whelping.<sup about="#mwt1063" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Alderton_181-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"r","href":"./Template:R"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Alderton"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Alderton-181" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 181;" id="mwBJk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBJo">[181]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mwBJs"><i id="mwBJw">Whelping</i> – the act of a bitch giving birth.<sup about="#mwt1066" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Alderton_181-4" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"r","href":"./Template:R"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Alderton"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Alderton-181" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 181;" id="mwBJ0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBJ4">[181]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mwBJ8"><i id="mwBKA">Whelps</i> – puppies still dependent upon their dam.<sup about="#mwt1069" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Alderton_181-5" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"r","href":"./Template:R"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Alderton"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Dog#cite_note-Alderton-181" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 181;" id="mwBKE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBKI">[181]</span></a></sup></li></ul>
